<p><b>Caracas</b> (<small>Spanish pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[kaˈɾakas]</a></span>; <small>locally </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[kaˈɾaːka]</a></span>), officially <b>Santiago de León de Caracas</b>, is the capital, the center of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Caracas" title="Greater Caracas"><b>Greater Caracas Area</b></a>, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Venezuela#Largest_cities_in_Venezuela" title="List of cities in Venezuela">largest</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>. Caracas is located along the <a href="/wiki/Guaire_River" title="Guaire River">Guaire River</a> in the northern part of the country, following the contours of the narrow Caracas Valley on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coastal_Range,_Venezuela" title="Coastal Range, Venezuela">Venezuelan coastal mountain range</a> (Cordillera de la Costa). Terrain suitable for building lies between 760 and 1,140 m (2,490 and 3,740 ft) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>. The valley is close to the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, separated from the coast by a steep 2,200-metre-high (7,200 ft) <a href="/wiki/Mountain_range" title="Mountain range">mountain range</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cerro_El_%C3%81vila" title="Cerro El Ávila">Cerro El Ávila</a>; to the south there are more hills and mountains.</p>
<p>The <b>Metropolitan District of Caracas</b> is made up of five municipalities: <a href="/wiki/Libertador_Bolivarian_Municipality" title="Libertador Bolivarian Municipality">Libertador Municipality</a> which is the only administrative division of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venezuelan_Capital_District" title="Venezuelan Capital District">Venezuelan Capital District</a>, and four other municipalities, which are within in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miranda_State" title="Miranda State">Miranda State</a>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chacao_Municipality" title="Chacao Municipality">Chacao</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baruta_Municipality" title="Baruta Municipality">Baruta</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sucre_Municipality,_Miranda" title="Sucre Municipality, Miranda">Sucre</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Hatillo_Municipality,_Miranda" title="El Hatillo Municipality, Miranda">El Hatillo</a>. Libertador holds many of the government buildings and is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venezuelan_Capital_District" title="Venezuelan Capital District">Capital District</a> (<i>Distrito Capital</i>). The Distrito Capital had a population of 2,013,366 as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cabildo_Metropolitano_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cabildo_Metropolitano-3">[3]</a></sup> while the Metropolitan District of Caracas was estimated at 3,273,863 as of 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cabildo_Metropolitano_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cabildo_Metropolitano-3">[3]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Region_of_Caracas" title="Metropolitan Region of Caracas">Metropolitan Region of Caracas</a> has an estimated population of 5,243,301.</p>
<p>Businesses in the city include service companies, banks, and malls. Caracas has a largely service-based economy, apart from some industrial activity in its metropolitan area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caracas_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Caracas-4">[4]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Caracas_Stock_Exchange" title="Caracas Stock Exchange">Caracas Stock Exchange</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petr%C3%B3leos_de_Venezuela" title="Petróleos de Venezuela">Petróleos de Venezuela</a> (PDVSA) are headquartered in Caracas. PDVSA is the largest company in Venezuela. Caracas is also Venezuela's cultural capital, with many restaurants, theaters, museums, and <a href="/wiki/Shopping" title="Shopping">shopping</a> centers. Some of the tallest skyscrapers in Latin America are located in Caracas.</p>
<p>In 2015, Caracas had the highest per capita murder rates in the world, with 119 homicides per 100,000 inhabitants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Most murders and other violent crimes go unsolved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Caracas" title="Timeline of Caracas">Timeline of Caracas</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">

<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diego_de_Losada_-_Antonio_Herrera_Toro_Concejo_Municipal_de_Caracas.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1476" data-file-width="772" height="325" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Diego_de_Losada_-_Antonio_Herrera_Toro_Concejo_Municipal_de_Caracas.jpg/170px-Diego_de_Losada_-_Antonio_Herrera_Toro_Concejo_Municipal_de_Caracas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Diego_de_Losada_-_Antonio_Herrera_Toro_Concejo_Municipal_de_Caracas.jpg/255px-Diego_de_Losada_-_Antonio_Herrera_Toro_Concejo_Municipal_de_Caracas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Diego_de_Losada_-_Antonio_Herrera_Toro_Concejo_Municipal_de_Caracas.jpg/340px-Diego_de_Losada_-_Antonio_Herrera_Toro_Concejo_Municipal_de_Caracas.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diego_de_Losada_-_Antonio_Herrera_Toro_Concejo_Municipal_de_Caracas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Conqueror <a href="/wiki/Diego_de_Losada" title="Diego de Losada">Diego de Losada</a>, founder of Santiago de León de Caracas (painted early 20th century )</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the time of the founding of the city in 1567,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> the valley of Caracas was populated by indigenous peoples. <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Fajardo" title="Francisco Fajardo">Francisco Fajardo</a>, the son of a Spanish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Captain_(land)" title="Captain (land)">captain</a> and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guaiqueri" title="Guaiqueri">Guaiqueri</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">cacica</a></i>, attempted to establish a plantation in the valley in 1562 after founding a series of coastal towns. Fajardo's settlement did not last long. It was destroyed by natives of the region led by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Terepaima&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Terepaima (page does not exist)">Terepaima</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guaicaipuro" title="Guaicaipuro">Guaicaipuro</a>. This was the last rebellion on the part of the natives. On <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/25_July" title="25 July">25 July</a> 1567, Captain <a href="/wiki/Diego_de_Losada" title="Diego de Losada">Diego de Losada</a> laid the foundations of the city of <i>Santiago de León de Caracas</i>. The foundation − 1567 – "I take possession of this land in the name of God and the King" These were the words of Don Diego de Losada in founding the city of Caracas on 25 July 1567. In 1577 Caracas became the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Venezuela_Province" title="Venezuela Province">Venezuela Province</a> under Governor <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Pimentel" title="Juan de Pimentel">Juan de Pimentel</a> (1576–1583).</p>
<p>During the 17th century, the coast of Venezuela was frequently raided by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pirate" title="Pirate">pirates</a>. With the coastal mountains as a barrier, Caracas was relatively immune to such attacks. However, <a href="/wiki/Preston_Somers_Expedition" title="Preston Somers Expedition">in 1595</a>, around 200 English privateers including George Sommers and Amyas Preston crossed the mountains through a little-used pass while the town's defenders were guarding the more often-used one. Encountering little resistance, the invaders sacked and set fire to the town after a failed ransom negotiation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the cocoa cultivation and exports under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Compa%C3%B1%C3%ADa_Guipuzcoana_de_Caracas" title="Compañía Guipuzcoana de Caracas">Compañía Guipuzcoana de Caracas</a> grew in importance, the city expanded. In 1777, Caracas became the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Venezuela" title="Captaincy General of Venezuela">Captaincy General of Venezuela</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Thomas_1839_000.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1932" data-file-width="3060" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Joseph_Thomas_1839_000.jpg/260px-Joseph_Thomas_1839_000.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Joseph_Thomas_1839_000.jpg/390px-Joseph_Thomas_1839_000.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Joseph_Thomas_1839_000.jpg/520px-Joseph_Thomas_1839_000.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Thomas_1839_000.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Caracas, as painted by Joseph Thomas in 1839</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Espa%C3%B1a&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="José María España (page does not exist)">José María España</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Manuel_Gual&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Manuel Gual (page does not exist)">Manuel Gual</a> led an attempted revolution aimed at independence, but the rebellion was put down on 13 July 1797. Caracas was ultimately the site of the signing of a <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_independence" title="Declaration of independence">Declaration of Independence</a> on 5 July 1811. In 1812, an <a href="/wiki/1812_Caracas_earthquake" title="1812 Caracas earthquake">earthquake destroyed Caracas</a>. The independentist war continued until 24 June 1821, when Bolívar defeated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royalist_(Hispanic_American_Revolution)" title="Royalist (Hispanic American Revolution)">royalists</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Carabobo" title="Battle of Carabobo">Battle of Carabobo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HT_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-HT-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Caracas,_Venezuela.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3368" data-file-width="4464" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Caracas%2C_Venezuela.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Caracas%2C_Venezuela.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Caracas%2C_Venezuela.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Caracas%2C_Venezuela.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Caracas%2C_Venezuela.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Caracas%2C_Venezuela.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caracas,_Venezuela.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Caracas cityscape in the early 1900s.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Caracas grew in economic importance during Venezuela's oil boom in the early 20th century. During the 1950s, Caracas began an intensive modernization program which continued throughout the 1960s and early 1970s. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universidad_Central_de_Venezuela" title="Universidad Central de Venezuela">Universidad Central de Venezuela</a>, designed by modernist architect <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Ra%C3%BAl_Villanueva" title="Carlos Raúl Villanueva">Carlos Raúl Villanueva</a> and declared <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage" title="World Heritage">World Heritage</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>, was built. New working- and middle-class residential districts sprouted in the valley, extending the urban area toward the east and southeast. Joining <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=El_Silencio(Caracas)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="El Silencio(Caracas) (page does not exist)">El Silencio</a>, also designed by Villanueva, were several workers' housing districts, 23 de Enero and Simon Rodriguez. Middle-class developments include Bello Monte, Los Palos Grandes, Chuao, and El Cafetal. The dramatic change in the economic structure of the country, which went from being primarily agricultural to dependent on oil production, stimulated the fast development of Caracas, and made it a magnet for people in rural communities who migrated to the capital city in an unplanned fashion searching for greater economic opportunity. This migration created the <i>rancho</i> (slum) belt of the valley of Caracas.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Caracas.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="429" data-file-width="349" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Caracas.gif/170px-Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Caracas.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Caracas.gif/255px-Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Caracas.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Caracas.gif/340px-Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Caracas.gif 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Caracas.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Colonial painting of Our Lady of Caracas, Patroness of the city</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The flag of Caracas consists of a burgundy red field with the version of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coat_of_Arms" title="Coat of Arms">Coat of Arms</a> of the City (effective since the 1980s). The red field symbolises the blood spilt by Caraquenian people in favour of independence and the highest ideals of the Venezuelan Nation. Later, in the year 1994, presumably as a result of the change of municipal authorities, it was decided to increase the size of the Caracas coat of arms and move it to the centre of the field. This version of the flag is still in use today.</p>
<p>The coat of arms of the City of Caracas was adopted by the <a href="/wiki/Libertador_Bolivarian_Municipality" title="Libertador Bolivarian Municipality">Libertador Municipality</a> to identify itself. Later, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Metropolitan_Mayor_Office&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Metropolitan Mayor Office (page does not exist)">Metropolitan Mayor Office</a> assumed the lion, the scallop and <a href="/wiki/Cross_of_Saint_James" title="Cross of Saint James">Saint James' Cross</a> for the same purpose.</p>
<p>The anthem of the city is the <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Marcha_a_Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Marcha a Caracas (page does not exist)">Marcha a Caracas</a></i>, written by the composer <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tiero_Pezzuti_de_Matteis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tiero Pezzuti de Matteis (page does not exist)">Tiero Pezzuti de Matteis</a> with the lyrics by <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Enrique_Sarabia" title="José Enrique Sarabia">José Enrique Sarabia</a>. The lyrics are said to be inspired by the heroism of the Caraquenian people, and the memory of the <i>City of Red Roofs</i>. Incidentally, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Anthem" title="National Anthem">National Anthem</a> of Venezuela, <i><a href="/wiki/Gloria_al_Bravo_Pueblo" title="Gloria al Bravo Pueblo">Gloria al Bravo Pueblo</a></i>, includes the lines "...y si el despotismo levanta la voz, seguid el ejemplo que Caracas dio" ("...and if despotism raises its voice, follow the example that Caracas gave"), reflecting the fact that, in addition to generously providing many heroic fighters to the War of Independence, the junta established in Caracas (19 April 1810) served as inspiration for other regions to do the same—as did its <a href="/wiki/Venezuelan_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Venezuelan Declaration of Independence">declaration of independence</a> a year later.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Caracas has five municipalities: Baruta, El Hatillo, Chacao, Libertador and Sucre. Under the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Venezuela" title="Constitution of Venezuela">constitution of Venezuela</a>, municipal governments have two branches: the executive (governed by a mayor) and the legislative (managed by a <a href="/wiki/Municipal_council" title="Municipal council">municipal council</a>). On 8 March 2000, the year after a new constitution was introduced in Venezuela, it was <a href="/wiki/Decree" title="Decree">decreed</a> in <i>Gaceta Official</i> N° 36,906 that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_District_of_Caracas" title="Metropolitan District of Caracas">Metropolitan District of Caracas</a> would be created, and that some of the powers of these municipalities would be delegated to the <i>Alcaldía Mayor</i>, physically located in the large Libertador municipality, in the center of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Edificio_BVC.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Edificio_BVC.jpg/170px-Edificio_BVC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Edificio_BVC.jpg/255px-Edificio_BVC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Edificio_BVC.jpg/340px-Edificio_BVC.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Edificio_BVC.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Caracas_Stock_Exchange" title="Caracas Stock Exchange">Caracas Stock Exchange</a> building in <a href="/wiki/El_Rosal,_Caracas" title="El Rosal, Caracas">El Rosal</a> district</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Businesses that are located here include service companies, banks, and malls, among others. It has a largely service-based economy, apart from some industrial activity in its metropolitan area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caracas_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Caracas-4">[4]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Caracas_Stock_Exchange" title="Caracas Stock Exchange">Caracas Stock Exchange</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petr%C3%B3leos_de_Venezuela" title="Petróleos de Venezuela">Petróleos de Venezuela</a> (PDVSA) are headquartered here. The PDVSA is the largest company in Venezuela,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> and negotiates all the <a href="/wiki/Treaty" title="Treaty">international agreements</a> for the distribution and export of petroleum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> When the company existed, the airline <a href="/wiki/Viasa" title="Viasa">Viasa</a> had its headquarters in the Torre Viasa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Caracas' central business district is Milla de Oro, which is located in the north of the Baruta municipality and the south of the Chacao municipality, it is one of largest financial districts of Latin America, it is home to many companies and is dominated by numerous high-rises. Other important business districts include Plaza Venezuela, Parque Central Complex and El Recreo.</p>
<p>Small and medium-size industry contributes to the Caracas economy. The city provides communication and transportation infrastructure between the metropolitan area and the rest of the country. Important industries in Caracas include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chemicals" title="Chemicals">chemicals</a>, textiles, leather, <a href="/wiki/Food_industry" title="Food industry">food</a>, iron and wood products. There are also rubber and cement factories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Its GDP(Nominal) is 70 billion USD and the GDP(PPP) per Capita is.USD 24,000 <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cost_of_living">Cost of living</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Cost of living">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A 2009 United Nations survey reported that the <a href="/wiki/Cost_of_living" title="Cost of living">cost of living</a> in Caracas was 89% of that of its baseline city: New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> However, this statistic is based upon a fixed currency-exchange-rate of 2003 and might not be completely realistic, due to the elevated inflation rates of the last several years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Precise_language" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The text near this tag is dated.">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2013, the World Economic forum evaluated countries in terms of how successful they were in advertising campaigns to attract foreign visitors. Out of the 140 countries evaluated, Venezuela fell in the last place. There are multiple factors that contribute to the lack of tourism in Caracas. A major factor that has contributed to the lack of foreign visitors has been poor transport for tourists. Venezuela has limited railway systems and airlines. High crime rates and the negative attitude of the Venezuelan population towards tourism also contributed to the poor evaluation.</p>
<p>In an attempt to attract more foreign visitors, the Venezuelan Ministry of Tourism invested in multiple hotel infrastructures. The largest hotel investment has been in the Hotel Alba Caracas. The cost for the general maintenance of the north and south towers of the hotel is approximately 231.5 million Venezuelan bolivars.</p>
<p>Although the Venezuelan Ministry of Tourism has taken the initiative to recognize the importance of the tourism industry, the Venezuelan government has not placed the tourism industry as an economic priority. In 2013, the budget for the Ministry of Tourism was only 173.8 million bolivars, while the Ministry of the Youth received approximately 724.6 million bolivars.</p>
<p>The tourism industry in Venezuela contributes approximately 3.8 percent of the country GDP. Venezuela's current goal is to reach a GDP of 7.6 percent. The World Economic Forum predicts Venezuela's GDP to rise to 4.2 percent by 2022.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Caracas is contained entirely within a valley of the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_de_la_Costa_Central" title="Cordillera de la Costa Central">Venezuelan central range</a>, and separated from the Caribbean coast by a roughly 15 kilometres (9 miles) expanse of <a href="/wiki/El_%C3%81vila_National_Park" title="El Ávila National Park">El Ávila National Park</a>. The valley is relatively small and quite irregular, the altitude with respect to sea level varies from between 870 and 1,043 meters (2,854 and 3,422 ft), with 900 meters (3,000 feet) in the historic zone. This, along with the rapid population growth, has profoundly influenced the <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning" title="Urban planning">urban development</a> of the city. The most elevated point of the Capital District, wherein the city is located, is the <i>Pico El Ávila</i>, which rises to 2,159 meters (7,083 feet). The main body of water in Caracas is the <a href="/wiki/Guaire_River" title="Guaire River">Guaire River</a>, which flows across the city and empties into the <i><a href="/wiki/Tuy_River" title="Tuy River">Tuy River</a></i>, which is also fed by the <i>El Valle</i> and <i>San Pedro</i> rivers, in addition to numerous streams which descend from El Ávila. The <i>La Mariposa</i> and <i>Camatagua</i> reservoirs provide water to the city. The city is occasionally subject to earthquakes - notably in 1641 and 1967.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Este_de_Caracas.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Este_de_Caracas.JPG/220px-Este_de_Caracas.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Este_de_Caracas.JPG/330px-Este_de_Caracas.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Este_de_Caracas.JPG/440px-Este_de_Caracas.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Este_de_Caracas.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of the east side of Caracas</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Under the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>, Caracas has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">tropical savanna climate</a> (Aw). Caracas is also intertropical, with precipitation that varies between 900 and 1,300 millimeters (35 and 51 inches) (annual), in the city proper, and up to 2,000 millimeters (79 inches) in some parts of the Mountain range. While Caracas is within the tropics, due to its altitude temperatures are generally not nearly as high as other tropical locations at sea level. The annual average temperature is approximately 23.8 °C (75 °F), with the average of the coldest month (January) 22.8 °C (73 °F) and the average of the warmest month (July) 25.0 °C (77 °F), which gives a small annual thermal amplitude of 2.2 °C (4.0 °F). In the months of December and January abundant fog may appear, in addition to a sudden nightly drop in temperature, until reaching 8 °C (46 °F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> This peculiar weather is known by the natives of Caracas as the <i>Pacheco</i>. In addition, nightly temperatures at any time of the year are much (14 to 20 °C) lower than daytime highs and usually do not remain above <span style="white-space:nowrap">24 °C (75 °F)</span>, resulting in very pleasant evening temperatures. Hail storms appear in Caracas, although only on rare occasions. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrical_storm" title="Electrical storm">Electrical storms</a> are much more frequent, especially between June and October, due to the city being in a closed valley and the orographic action of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cerro_El_%C3%81vila" title="Cerro El Ávila">Cerro El Ávila</a>. Caracas record extremes have been reported in other city's stations to reach a minimum of 6 °C (43 °F) and a maximum of 35.5 °C (95.9 °F)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (February 2017)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Self-published_sources" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="This reference citation appears to be to a self-published source. (February 2017)">self-published source</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to the population census of 2011 the Caracas proper (Distrito Capital) is over 1.9 million inhabitants,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ine.gov.ve_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-ine.gov.ve-28">[28]</a></sup> while that of the Metropolitan District of Caracas is estimated at 2.9 million as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. The majority of the population is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mixed_Race" title="Mixed Race">mixed-race</a>, typically with varying degrees of <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">European</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_ethnic_groups_of_Africa" title="List of ethnic groups of Africa">African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Indigenous</a> and occasional <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Asia" title="Ethnic groups in Asia">Asian</a> ancestry. There is a noteworthy <a href="/wiki/Afro-Venezuelan" title="Afro-Venezuelan">Afro-Venezuelan</a> community formed by residents whose ancestors settled in Caracas after being liberated from <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">slavery</a> as a reward for aiding Bolívar in the <a href="/wiki/Venezuelan_War_of_Independence" title="Venezuelan War of Independence">Venezuelan War of Independence</a>. Additionally, the city has a large number of both European Venezuelans &amp; Asian Venezuelans who descend from the massive influx of various immigrants Venezuela received from all across Eurasia during the 20th century. The descendants of Spaniards, Portuguese, Italians, Chinese, Colombians, Germans, Syrians and Lebanese stand out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ine.gov.ve_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-ine.gov.ve-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:802px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CaracasAvila.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="758" data-file-width="2000" height="303" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/CaracasAvila.jpg/800px-CaracasAvila.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/CaracasAvila.jpg/1200px-CaracasAvila.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/CaracasAvila.jpg/1600px-CaracasAvila.jpg 2x" width="800"/></a>

Panoramic view of the Caracas valley from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parque_Nacional_El_%C3%81vila" title="Parque Nacional El Ávila">Parque Nacional El Ávila</a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:802px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panoramic_view_of_Caracas_night.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1327" data-file-width="4037" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Panoramic_view_of_Caracas_night.jpg/800px-Panoramic_view_of_Caracas_night.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Panoramic_view_of_Caracas_night.jpg/1200px-Panoramic_view_of_Caracas_night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Panoramic_view_of_Caracas_night.jpg/1600px-Panoramic_view_of_Caracas_night.jpg 2x" width="800"/></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Petare_Slums_in_Caracas.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2496" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Petare_Slums_in_Caracas.jpg/250px-Petare_Slums_in_Caracas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Petare_Slums_in_Caracas.jpg/375px-Petare_Slums_in_Caracas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Petare_Slums_in_Caracas.jpg/500px-Petare_Slums_in_Caracas.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Petare_Slums_in_Caracas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The slums on the east and west hills of Caracas are the poorest neighborhoods in the city, and where crime tends to be concentrated.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Venezuela and its capital, Caracas, are reported to both have among the highest per capita murder rates in the world. Caracas is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_murder_rate" title="List of cities by murder rate">city with the highest homicide rate in the world outside of a warzone</a>, with a 2016 rate of around 120 murders per 100,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seguridadjusticiaypaz_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-seguridadjusticiaypaz-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Consejo_Ciudadano_para_la_Seguridad_P.C3.BAblica_y_la_Justicia_Penal_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Consejo_Ciudadano_para_la_Seguridad_P.C3.BAblica_y_la_Justicia_Penal-35">[35]</a></sup> Most murders and other violent crimes go unsolved, with estimates of the number of unresolved crimes as high as 98%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_State" title="U.S. Department of State">U.S. Department of State</a> has issued <a href="/wiki/Travel_warning" title="Travel warning">travel warnings</a> for Venezuela (especially Caracas) due to high rates of crime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_Capitol">Federal Capitol</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Federal Capitol">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Palacio_Federal_Legislativo" title="Palacio Federal Legislativo">Federal Capitol</a> occupies an entire <a href="/wiki/City_block" title="City block">city block</a>, and, with its golden domes and neoclassical pediments, can seem even bigger. The building was commissioned by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Guzm%C3%A1n_Blanco" title="Antonio Guzmán Blanco">Antonio Guzmán Blanco</a> in the 1870s, and is most famous for its <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sal%C3%B3n_El%C3%ADptico&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Salón Elíptico (page does not exist)">Salón Elíptico</a>, an oval hall with a mural-covered dome and walls lined with portraits of the country's great and good. The nearby <a href="/wiki/Palacio_Municipal_de_Caracas" title="Palacio Municipal de Caracas">Palacio Municipal de Caracas</a> dating from 1696 was renovated in the <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">Neoclassical style</a> in 1906 and now serves as the city hall and the Caracas Museum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecu_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-ecu-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Park">East Park</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: East Park">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Caracas East Park (<i><a href="/wiki/Parque_del_Este" title="Parque del Este">Parque del Este</a></i>, now officially <i>Parque Generalísimo Francisco de Miranda</i>) was designed by Brazilian architect <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Burle_Marx" title="Roberto Burle Marx">Roberto Burle Marx</a>. It is a green paradise in the middle of the city, and it contains a small zoo. A replica of the ship led by <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Miranda" title="Francisco de Miranda">Francisco de Miranda</a>, the <i>Leander</i>, is in the southern part of the park. Before there used to exist a replica of the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_(ship)" title="Santa María (ship)">Santa Maria</a> ship, used by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christopher_Colombus" title="Christopher Colombus">Christopher Colombus</a> in his voyages to America.</p>
<h3><span id="Teresa_Carreño_Cultural_Complex"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Teresa_Carre.C3.B1o_Cultural_Complex">Teresa Carreño Cultural Complex</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Teresa Carreño Cultural Complex">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Teresa_Carre%C3%B1o_Cultural_Complex" title="Teresa Carreño Cultural Complex">Teresa Carreño Cultural Complex</a></div>
<p>The <b><a href="/wiki/Teresa_Carre%C3%B1o_Cultural_Complex" title="Teresa Carreño Cultural Complex">Teresa Carreño Cultural Complex</a></b> (<i>Complejo Cultural Teresa Carreño</i>), or more commonly the <b>Teresa Carreño Theatre</b> (<i>Teatro Teresa Carreño</i>), is by far the most important theater of Caracas and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>. The theater presents symphonic and popular concerts, operas, ballet, and dramatic works. It is the second largest theater in South America, after the <a href="/wiki/Teatro_Col%C3%B3n" title="Teatro Colón">Teatro Colón</a> of <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, Argentina.</p>
<h3><span id="Simón_Bolívar's_Birthplace_Home"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sim.C3.B3n_Bol.C3.ADvar.27s_Birthplace_Home">Simón Bolívar's Birthplace Home</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Simón Bolívar's Birthplace Home">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Skyscrapers may loom overhead, but there is more than a hint of original colonial flavor in this neatly proportioned reconstruction of the house where <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a> was born on 24 July 1783. The museum's exhibits include period <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weapons" title="Weapons">weapons</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Banners" title="Banners">banners</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uniforms" title="Uniforms">uniforms</a>.</p>
<p>Much of the original colonial interior has been replaced by monumental paintings of battle scenes, but more personal <a href="/wiki/Relic" title="Relic">relics</a> can be seen in the nearby <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivarian_Museum_of_Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bolivarian Museum of Caracas (page does not exist)">Bolivarian museum</a>. The pride of the place goes to the coffin in which Bolívar's remains were brought from <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>; his ashes now rest in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pante%C3%B3n_Nacional" title="Panteón Nacional">National Pantheon</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Pantheon">National Pantheon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: National Pantheon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/National_Pantheon_of_Venezuela" title="National Pantheon of Venezuela">National Pantheon of Venezuela</a></div>
<p>Venezuela's most venerated building is five blocks north of Plaza Bolívar, on the northern edge of the old town. Formerly a church, the building was given its new purpose as the final resting place for eminent Venezuelans by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Guzm%C3%A1n_Blanco" title="Antonio Guzmán Blanco">Antonio Guzmán Blanco</a> in 1874.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parque_Central_Complex">Parque Central Complex</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Parque Central Complex">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Parque_Central_Complex" title="Parque Central Complex">Parque Central Complex</a></div>
<p>At a short distance east of Plaza Bolívar is Parque Central, a concrete complex of five high-rise residential slabs of somewhat apocalyptic-appearing architecture, crowned by two 56-storey octagonal towers, one of them is under repair due to the fire which burnt the building on 17 October 2004.</p>
<p>Parque Central is Caracas' art and culture hub, with museums, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movie_theatre" title="Movie theatre">cinemas</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Teresa_Carre%C3%B1o_Cultural_Complex" title="Teresa Carreño Cultural Complex">Teresa Carreño Cultural Complex</a>. The West Tower balcony, on the 52nd floor, gives a 360° bird's-eye view of Caracas.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_squares">Public squares</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Public squares">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><i>Plaza Bolívar</i> is the focus of the old town with the monument to <i>El Libertador</i>, Simón Bolívar, at its heart. Modern high-rise buildings have overpowered much of the colonial flavor of Caracas' founding neighbourhood.</li>
<li><i>Plaza Venezuela</i> is the geographic center of Caracas. It is a large urban plaza at the entrance of the Central University of Venezuela. Kinetic artists have displayed their works there, including <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Cruz-Diez" title="Carlos Cruz-Diez">Carlos Cruz-Diez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Otero" title="Alejandro Otero">Alejandro Otero</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesus_Soto" title="Jesus Soto">Jesus Soto</a>. East of the Plaza is the Plaza Venezuela Fountain, a large computerized display of water, music and colored light refurbished in 2009 to include the latest available technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Plaza Caracas</i> was constructed in 1983. It is in the Simón Bolívar Center.</li>
<li><i>Plaza San Jacinto</i> dates to 1603 and used to be the site of the city market</li>
<li><i>Plaza Los Palos Grandes</i> is a modern construction located at the municipality of Chacao. It has a display of water and a beautiful coffee shop. this plaza is the center of free yoga lessons for all the people that want to enjoy the city outdoors. It also has its own library.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="El_Hatillo">El Hatillo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: El Hatillo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Hatillo_Municipality" title="El Hatillo Municipality">El Hatillo Municipality</a></div>
<p>El Hatillo is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonisation" title="Colonisation">colonial</a> town that is located at the south-east suburbs of Caracas in the municipal area of the same name. This small town, which is one of Venezuela's few well-preserved typical colonial areas, gives an idea of what Caracas was like in centuries past.</p>
<h3><span id="Cerro_El_Ávila"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cerro_El_.C3.81vila">Cerro El Ávila</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Cerro El Ávila">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cerro_El_%C3%81vila" title="Cerro El Ávila">Cerro El Ávila</a></div>
<p><i>Cerro El Ávila</i> (<i>Mountain El Ávila</i>) (Indigenous name: Waraira Repano), is a mountain in the mid-North of Venezuela. It rises next to Caracas and separates the city from the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>. It is considered the lungs of Caracas due to the amount of vegetation on the mountain.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Las_Mercedes">Las Mercedes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Las Mercedes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Las_Mercedes_(district_in_Caracas,_Venezuela)" title="Las Mercedes (district in Caracas, Venezuela)">Las Mercedes (district in Caracas, Venezuela)</a></div>
<p>This zone contains restaurants with varied gastronomical specialties, along with pubs, bars, pools and art galleries.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Altamira_neighborhood">Altamira neighborhood</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Altamira neighborhood">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Altamira_(Caracas)" title="Altamira (Caracas)">Altamira (Caracas)</a></div>
<p>Altamira is a neighborhood in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chacao_Municipality,_Miranda" title="Chacao Municipality, Miranda">Chacao</a> municipality of Caracas. It has its own <a href="/wiki/Caracas_Metro" title="Caracas Metro">Metro Station</a>, many hotels, malls and restaurants, and is an important business and cultural centre. The <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Miranda" title="Francisco de Miranda">Francisco de Miranda</a> avenue (a major avenue in Caracas) and the Distibuidor Altamira (a congested <a href="/wiki/Interchange_(road)" title="Interchange (road)">highway exit</a>) are both in Altamira.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_buildings">Religious buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religious buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Iglesia_de_San_Francisco_(Caracas)" title="Iglesia de San Francisco (Caracas)">Iglesia de San Francisco</a> is of historical value. Bolívar's funeral was held here twelve years after his death. Here he was proclaimed <i><a href="/wiki/Title_of_honor" title="Title of honor">Libertador</a></i> in 1813 by the people of Caracas. The church has gilded <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">baroque</a> altarpieces, and retains much of its original colonial interior, despite being given a treatment in the 19th century under the auspices of <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Guzm%C3%A1n_Blanco" title="Antonio Guzmán Blanco">Antonio Guzmán Blanco</a>, which was intended to be modernizing.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It contains some 17th-century masterpieces of art, carvings, sculptures and oil paintings. The Central University of Venezuela, established during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">Philip V</a>, was lodged for centuries in the church cloisters next door, which today are the seat of the Language Academy, and the Academies of History, Physics, and Mathematics.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Caracas_Cathedral" title="Caracas Cathedral">Caracas Cathedral</a> is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Caracas" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Caracas">Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Caracas</a>. <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_St._Teresa" title="Basilica of St. Teresa">Basilica of St. Teresa</a> is designated a National Historic Landmark.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mosque_of_Sheikh_Ibrahim_Al-Ibrahim" title="Mosque of Sheikh Ibrahim Al-Ibrahim">Mosque of Sheikh Ibrahim Al-Ibrahim</a> is the second largest mosque in Latin America. For many years it was the biggest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="external text" href="http://www.uic.org.ve" rel="nofollow">Union Israelita de Caracas</a> is the biggest Synagogue for the Jewish Ashkenazi community in Caracas. Its mission is to host the religious services and preserve the memory of the Jewish heritage in Venezuela. Similarly, Mariperez is the biggest Synagogue for the Jewish Sephardic community in Caracas.</p>

<h2><span id="Colleges,_universities_and_international_schools"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges.2C_universities_and_international_schools">Colleges, universities and international schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Colleges, universities and international schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_University_of_Venezuela">Central University of Venezuela</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Central University of Venezuela">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Central_University_of_Venezuela" title="Central University of Venezuela">Central University of Venezuela</a></div>
<p>The Central University of Venezuela (<i>Universidad Central de Venezuela</i> in Spanish) is a public University. Founded in 1721, it is the oldest university in Venezuela and one of the first in Latin America.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The university campus was designed by architect <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Ra%C3%BAl_Villanueva" title="Carlos Raúl Villanueva">Carlos Raúl Villanueva</a> and it was declared <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage" title="World Heritage">World Heritage</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> in 2000. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ciudad_Universitaria_de_Caracas" title="Ciudad Universitaria de Caracas">Ciudad Universitaria de Caracas</a>, as the main Campus is also known, is considered a masterpiece of architecture and urban planning and it is the only university campus designed in the 20th century that has received such recognition by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span id="Simón_Bolívar_University"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sim.C3.B3n_Bol.C3.ADvar_University">Simón Bolívar University</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Simón Bolívar University">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar_University" title="Simón Bolívar University">Simón Bolívar University</a></div>
<p>The Simón Bolívar University (Universidad Simón Bolívar, in Spanish, or USB) is a public institution in Caracas that focuses on science and technology. Its motto is <i>"La Universidad de la Excelencia"</i> ("University of Excellence").</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Universitario-caracas.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1426" data-file-width="4612" height="68" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Universitario-caracas.jpg/220px-Universitario-caracas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Universitario-caracas.jpg/330px-Universitario-caracas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Universitario-caracas.jpg/440px-Universitario-caracas.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Universitario-caracas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Central_University_of_Venezuela" title="Central University of Venezuela">UCV</a> Baseball Stadium</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_(Caracas).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_%28Caracas%29.jpg/220px-Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_%28Caracas%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_%28Caracas%29.jpg/330px-Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_%28Caracas%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_%28Caracas%29.jpg/440px-Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_%28Caracas%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_(Caracas).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_(Caracas)" title="Estadio Olímpico (Caracas)">UCV Olympic Stadium</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city hosted the official <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2013_Americas_Basketball_Championship" title="2013 Americas Basketball Championship">2013 Americas Basketball Championship</a>.</p>
<p>There are professional association football, baseball and several other sports.</p>
<p>Professional teams include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caracas_F%C3%BAtbol_Club" title="Caracas Fútbol Club">Caracas Fútbol Club</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deportivo_Petare" title="Deportivo Petare">Deportivo Petare</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atletico_Venezuela" title="Atletico Venezuela">Atletico Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/SD_Centro_Italo_Venezolano" title="SD Centro Italo Venezolano">SD Centro Italo Venezolano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estrella_Roja_FC" title="Estrella Roja FC">Estrella Roja FC</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Esppor_Club" title="Real Esppor Club">Real Esppor Club</a>. The Deportivo Petare has reached the semifinals of international tournaments, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copa_Libertadores_de_America" title="Copa Libertadores de America">Copa Libertadores de America</a>, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caracas_F%C3%BAtbol_Club" title="Caracas Fútbol Club">Caracas Fútbol Club</a> has reached the quarterfinals.</p>
<p>Baseball teams <a href="/wiki/Tiburones_de_La_Guaira" title="Tiburones de La Guaira">Tiburones de La Guaira</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leones_del_Caracas" title="Leones del Caracas">Leones del Caracas</a> play in the <i>Estadio Universitario de la UCV</i>, of the <a href="/wiki/Central_University_of_Venezuela" title="Central University of Venezuela">Central University of Venezuela</a>, with a capacity of 26,000 spectators.</p>
<p>Another baseball team started in Caracas: the <a href="/wiki/Navegantes_del_Magallanes" title="Navegantes del Magallanes">Navegantes del Magallanes</a>. It was moved to <a href="/wiki/Valencia,_Carabobo" title="Valencia, Carabobo">Valencia, Carabobo</a> in the 1970s.</p>
<p>Association Football stadiums include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_(Caracas)" title="Estadio Olímpico (Caracas)">Estadio Olímpico de la UCV</a>, with capacity of 30 000 spectators is seat of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deportivo_Italia" title="Deportivo Italia">Deportivo Italia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caracas_F%C3%BAtbol_Club" title="Caracas Fútbol Club">Caracas Fútbol Club</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Estadio_Br%C3%ADgido_Iriarte" title="Estadio Brígido Iriarte">Brígido Iriarte stadium</a>, with a capacity of 12 000 spectators (old seat of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deportivo_Italia" title="Deportivo Italia">Deportivo Italia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caracas_F%C3%BAtbol_Club" title="Caracas Fútbol Club">Caracas Fútbol Club</a>, and seat of the <a href="/wiki/Estrella_Roja_FC" title="Estrella Roja FC">Estrella Roja FC</a>). The Caracas Fútbol Club opened its own stadium in 2005, <i>Campo Deportivo Cocodrilos</i>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cocodrilos_de_Caracas" title="Cocodrilos de Caracas">Cocodrilos de Caracas</a> plays in the Venezuelan professional basketball league. They play their games in the "Gimnasio José Beracasa" in the neighbourhood of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=El_Para%C3%ADso,_Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="El Paraíso, Caracas (page does not exist)">El Paraíso</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>Caracas is the seat of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=National_Institute_of_Sports_(Venezuela)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="National Institute of Sports (Venezuela) (page does not exist)">National Institute of Sports</a> and of the Venezuelan <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">Olympic Committee</a>.</p>
<p>Caracas hosted the <a href="/wiki/1983_Pan_American_Games" title="1983 Pan American Games">1983 Pan American Games</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Teams">Teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Association Football: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caracas_F%C3%BAtbol_Club" title="Caracas Fútbol Club">Caracas Fútbol Club</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deportivo_Petare" title="Deportivo Petare">Deportivo Petare</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atletico_Venezuela" title="Atletico Venezuela">Atletico Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/SD_Centro_Italo_Venezolano" title="SD Centro Italo Venezolano">SD Centro Italo Venezolano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estrella_Roja_FC" title="Estrella Roja FC">Estrella Roja Futbol club</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Esppor_Club" title="Real Esppor Club">Real Esppor Club</a>.</li>
<li>Baseball: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiburones_de_la_Guaira" title="Tiburones de la Guaira">Tiburones de la Guaira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leones_del_Caracas" title="Leones del Caracas">Leones del Caracas</a>.</li>
<li>Basketball: <a href="/wiki/Cocodrilos_de_Caracas" title="Cocodrilos de Caracas">Cocodrilos de Caracas</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pastor_de_Nubes_o_Formes_de_Lutin.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Pastor_de_Nubes_o_Formes_de_Lutin.JPG/220px-Pastor_de_Nubes_o_Formes_de_Lutin.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Pastor_de_Nubes_o_Formes_de_Lutin.JPG/330px-Pastor_de_Nubes_o_Formes_de_Lutin.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Pastor_de_Nubes_o_Formes_de_Lutin.JPG/440px-Pastor_de_Nubes_o_Formes_de_Lutin.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pastor_de_Nubes_o_Formes_de_Lutin.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Cloud Shepherd</i>, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hans_Arp" title="Hans Arp">Hans Arp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_University_of_Venezuela" title="Central University of Venezuela">UCV</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Caracas is Venezuela's <a href="/wiki/Cultural_capital" title="Cultural capital">cultural capital</a>, with many restaurants, theaters, museums, and <a href="/wiki/Shopping" title="Shopping">shopping</a> centers. The city is home to an array of immigrants from but not limited to: Spain, Italy, Portugal, the Middle East, Germany, China, and Latin American countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gastronomy">Gastronomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Gastronomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Caracas has a gastronomical heritage due to the influence of immigrants, leading to a choice of regional and international cuisine. There are a variety of international restaurants including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_cuisine" title="American cuisine">American</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_cuisine" title="French cuisine">French</a>, Lebanese, <a href="/wiki/Italian_cuisine" title="Italian cuisine">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_cuisine" title="Spanish cuisine">Spanish</a>, Indian, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_cuisine" title="Chinese cuisine">Chinese</a>, Peruvian, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_cuisine" title="Japanese cuisine">Japanese</a>, Mediterranean and Mexican. The district of <i>La Candelaria</i> contains Spanish restaurants, resulting from Galician and Canarian immigrants that came to the area in the mid-20th century.</p>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iafetren.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Iafetren.JPG/220px-Iafetren.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Iafetren.JPG/330px-Iafetren.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Iafetren.JPG/440px-Iafetren.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iafetren.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Railway Caracas - Cúa</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Caracas_Metro" title="Caracas Metro">Caracas Metro</a> has been in operation since 27 March 1983. With 4 lines, 47 stations and about 10 more to be constructed. It covers a great part of the city and also has an integrated ticket system that combines the route of the <i>Metro</i> with those offered by the <i>Metrobús</i>, a bus service of the Caracas Metro. In 2010, the first segment of a new ariel cable car system opened, <a href="/wiki/Metrocable_(Caracas)" title="Metrocable (Caracas)">Metrocable</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> which feeds into the larger metro system.</li>
<li>Buses are the main means of <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">mass transportation</a>. There are two bus systems: the traditional system and the <i>Metrobús</i>. The traditional system runs a variety of bus types, operated by several companies on normal streets and avenues:
<ul>
<li>Autobus; large buses</li>
<li>Camioneta; medium size buses</li>
<li>microbus or camionetica; vans or minivans</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Instituto_Aut%C3%B3nomo_de_Ferrocarriles_del_Estado" title="Instituto Autónomo de Ferrocarriles del Estado">IFE</a>; train services to and from Tuy Valley cities of Charallave and Cúa</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar_International_Airport_(Venezuela)" title="Simón Bolívar International Airport (Venezuela)">Simón Bolívar International Airport</a>, the biggest and most important in the country is located outside the city, roughly 32 kilometres (20 mi) from the downtown area.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caracas_Aerial_Tramway" title="Caracas Aerial Tramway">Caracas Aerial Tramway</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Los_Teques_Metro" title="Los Teques Metro">Los Teques Metro</a> is a suburban mass-transit system completed in 2006 that connects Caracas with the suburban city of <a href="/wiki/Los_Teques" title="Los Teques">Los Teques</a>.</li>
<li>In March 2009 four of the five Caracas districts launched <i>Plan Vía Libre</i> to reduce traffic (the pro-Chavez <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Rodr%C3%ADguez_(politician)" title="Jorge Rodríguez (politician)">Jorge Rodríguez</a>' <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Libertador_Municipality_(Venezuelan_Capital_District)" title="Libertador Municipality (Venezuelan Capital District)">Libertador District</a> is currently not cooperating as the other districts are in the hands of the opposition<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>). On each weekday, cars with certain number plates are banned from entering key parts of the city centre; the numbers rotate so that any particular car is banned one day a week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></li>
<li>Generalisimo Francisco de Miranda airbase used by military aviation and govern aeroplane</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_South_America" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in South America">List of twin towns and sister cities in South America</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_Sister_Cities">Twin towns and Sister Cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Twin towns and Sister Cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Union_of_Ibero-American_Capital_Cities">Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caracas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Caracas is part of the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Ibero-American_Capital_Cities" title="Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities">Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> from 12 October 1982 establishing brotherly relations with the following cities:</p>
